<review>Premium doughnuts and chicken shack. I ordered the spicy birdy with cheese ( missing) and a chocolate glazed donut. The doughnut was super soft and had a great taste. Chocolate tasted smooth, no bitter or fake taste like some shops.

Spicy bird was center road spicy. It had a little build to it, so it's not punch you in the face hot. Pickles were not my thing and I am almost glad they forgot the cheese. Not sure if it's american or something else, since it wasn't in my sandwich. Chicken had a nice crunch and not over done.  Fries were good, not salty or much salt. Needed a dip or something.

Price was good shop was clean. Will likely head back for Nashville heat and maybe a different flavor doughnut. They had maple bacon and strawberry shortcake.

Update

Nashville is where it's at. It is the better üêî.</review>< time>

I used to live near and went to college next to their DTLA location and I would always go there to treat myself if I ever got really stressed from school. Their donuts and chicken sandwiches would always cheer me up.
I moved back to Corona and now my sister goes to college at Norco and I would pass by and always wondered if it was actually Birdies. I thought it was a knock off at first because why would one of the best and most popular donuts shop in LA be in Norco of all places?

< review>
Very clean and modern theater for live performances. The capacity is 516 so it is a very intimate experience. We saw James Garner tribute to Johnny Cash and it was phenomenal. No food or drink is allowed in the show, but at intermission they sell water and fresh baked cookies to help the high school fund raiser.<//review>

< Text>
Let's say "Liked it+". Definitely a high school auditorium, but it certainly beats seeing a play or performer in the high school gym as I used to do back in the '70s. The sound was decent/ not great, but the show was very good (well worth a ticket in the $40 -$55 bracket). Show wasn't sold out =no trouble finding a parking place; therefore, difficult to judge parking capacity had there been a "full house". Would I go there again? Yes. And it was nice to have a venue close to Hayward (it was Castro Valley).</Text>
